    "our formal fits to synthetic binaries ( see @xcite for details ) show that the most likely spectral types of the two components are l3.5@xmath60.7 and t2@xmath60.5 with estimated relative magnitudes of @xmath103 , @xmath104 , and @xmath105 mag .",
    "this object would be an excellent target for high - resolution imaging .",
    "we note that this object was also identified as a brown dwarf candidate by @xcite and given the designation sdss j131142.11 + 362923.9 .",
    "this object is tentatively classfied as y0 ( pec ? ) by cushing et al .",
    "( accepted ) , who describe its spectral features and derived physical parameters .",
    "we estimate a distance of 8.6 pc and find a high proper motion of 2.693@xmath60.398 arcsec / yr and high tangential velocity of 109.8@xmath616.2 km / s . as with most of the other y dwarf discoveries ,",
    "this object is detected by wise only in bands w2 and w3 and not in w1 or w4 ( table  [ wise_photometry_discoveries ] ) .",
    "the @xmath21-band spectrum of this object best fits the t8 standard , but there are discrepancies at @xmath29 and @xmath34 bands . at @xmath29 band",
    "the spectrum of wise 1436@xmath21814 shows excess flux relative to the standard , and at @xmath34 band the spectrum shows less flux relative to the standard ( figure  [ 1436m1814 ] ) .",
    "we therefore classify this object as a `` t8 pec '' . the physical cause ,",
    "as discussed above for several other objects , may be low metal content .",
    "this t6 dwarf is estimated to fall only 4.9 pc from the sun .",
    "its large motion ( @xmath1 = 1.388@xmath60.131 arcsec / yr ) placed it nearly in front of a star , now to the southeast , of similar near - infrared brightness during the 2mass survey ( see figure  [ finder_chart12 ] ) , and this confusion led to the source having been missed in photometric searches of the 2mass point source catalog .",
    "the near - infrared spectrum of this object , discussed in cushing et al .",
    "( accepted ) , is classified as y0 because of its similarity to the spectrum of the y0 near - infrared standard , wise 1738 + 2732 . as with most of the other y dwarf discoveries ,",
    "this object is detected by wise only in bands w2 and w3 and not in w1 or w4 ( table  [ wise_photometry_discoveries ] ) .",
    "in contrast to our crude spectrophotometric distance estimate from table  [ astrometry ] of 8.2 pc , we measure a trignometric parallax placing it at @xmath3 pc ( table  [ prelim_parallaxes ] ) , along with a proper motion of @xmath106 arcsec / yr .",
    "this parallax result is significant only at the 3@xmath100 level and is measured only over a 1.2yr baseline , so it should be treated as preliminary only .",
    "nonetheless , if confirmed , this distance would place wise 1541@xmath22250 as the seventh closest stellar system to the sun after the @xmath57 centauri system ( d=1.3 pc , @xcite ) , barnard s star ( d=1.8 pc , @xcite ) , wolf 359 ( d=2.4 pc , @xcite ) , lalande 21185 ( d=2.5 pc , @xcite ) , sirius ab ( d=2.6 pc , @xcite ) , and l 726 - 8 ab ( also known as bl ceti and uv ceti ; d=2.7 pc , @xcite )",
    ". the measured distance implies absolute magnitudes of @xmath78 and @xmath107 mag on the mko filter system and @xmath108 mag .",
    "this indicates a rapid dimming at those wavelengths in just a single spectral subclass from t9 to y0 ( see , e.g. , figure  [ mw2_vs_type ] and figure  [ mh_vs_type ] ) .",
    "the @xmath21-band spectrum of this object best fits the l9 standard , but there is excess flux at @xmath22 and particularly @xmath34 relative to the standard itself ( figure  [ 1647p5632 ] ) .",
    "we therefore classify this object as an `` l9 pec ( red ) '' .",
    "this object adds to a growing list of red l dwarfs whose red colors can not obviously be attributed to low gravity .",
    "it becomes the seventh example of this class , which now includes 2mass j21481633 + 4003594 and 2mass j18212815 + 1414010 from @xcite ; 2mass j13313310 + 3407583 , 2mass j23174712@xmath24838501 , and 2mass j23512200 + 3010540 from @xcite ; and wise 0206 + 2640 from above . as mentioned in @xcite ,",
    "the kinematics of the first five examples suggest that these objects derive from an old population , making them distinct from the red l dwarfs that have low - gravity spectral signatures and young kinematics .",
    "we note , however , that this object has a low tangential velocity of only 28.1@xmath61.2 km / s .",
    "however , this velocity assumes our spectrophotometric distance estimate of 20.2 pc , and our preliminary astrometric measurements over an 11.8yr baseline indicate a closer distance of @xmath109 pc , along with a motion of @xmath110 arcsec / yr . continued astrometric monitoring of this object is needed to see if this closer distance is confirmed , as this would provide another clue in deciphering the physical nature of this rare class of red ( non low-@xmath17 ) l dwarfs .",
    "cushing et al .  ( accepted ) propose this object as the y0 spectroscopic standard .",
    "it is the only one of our y dwarfs detected in all three short - wavelength bands of wise ( w1 , w2 , and w3 ) .",
    "our spectrophotometric distance estimate places it at 10.5 pc ; the available astrometry for this y0 dwarf spans barely six months ( table  [ astrometry ] ) , so we are not yet able to derive proper motion or parallax .",
    "this nearby dwarf of near - infrared spectral type t9 is detected in the 2mass and sdss surveys but was overlooked because of its weak detection in both . using a 10.4yr baseline , we find a high proper motion of @xmath1 = 1.555@xmath60.023 arcsec / yr and estimate a distance of 4.7 pc .",
    "our preliminary trigonometric parallax measurement places it at @xmath111 pc ( table  [ prelim_parallaxes ] ) . this object has identical optical and near - infrared types to another nearby object , ugps j072227.51@xmath2054031.2 , whose trigonometric parallax from @xcite places it at a distance of 4.1 pc .",
    "@xcite note that wise 1741 + 2553 appears single in near - infared imaging observations with laser guide star adaptive optics .",
    "the near - infrared spectrum of this object is classified as t9.5 : because of its similiarity to the spectrum of the t9.5 dwarf wise 0148@xmath27202 .",
    "although noisy , the narrowness of the j - band peaks falls intermediate between that of the t9 standard ugps j072227.51@xmath2054031.2 and the y0 standard wise 1738 + 2732 .",
    "we estimate that this object falls at a distance of 13.0 pc .",
    "the wise detections for this object are very similar to those seen for y dwarfs ; namely , the object is detected only in bands w2 and w3 and not in w1 or w4 ( table  [ wise_photometry_discoveries ] ) .",
    "this object , with a tentative classification of @xmath4y0 from cushing et al .",
    "( accepted ) , is the latest object so far found with wise .",
    "the spectrum is unique among late - t and y dwarfs in that the @xmath21- and @xmath22-band peaks , in units of @xmath112 , are nearly the same height ( figure  [ other_spectra_gt_t8 ] ) .",
    "this reddening of the near - infrared colors ( @xmath48 mag ; table  [ followup_photometry_discoveries ] ) is predicted by model atmosphere calculations to occur at effective temperatures below 300 - 400k ( @xcite ) .",
    "this effect is due to the fact that the wien tail of the spectral energy distribution becomes the overwhelming effect shaping the spectrum at those wavelengths , and this may be even more dramatically illustrated by the extremely red @xmath113 and @xmath114 colors measured for this object ( figure  [ jw2_vs_type ] and figure  [ hw2_vs_type ] ) .",
    "our spectrophotometric distance estimate of @xmath119.4 pc implies exceedingly dim absolute magnitudes of @xmath115 and @xmath116 mag , on the mko filter system .",
    "these values agree with expectations that wise 1828 + 2650 should be dimmer at these wavelengths than the presumably warmer wise 1541@xmath22250 , which also has exceedingly dim @xmath21 and @xmath22 magnitudes ( table  [ prelim_parallaxes ] ) .",
    "this y0 dwarf , discussed in cushing et al .",
    "( accepted ) , is estimated to lie at a distance of 7.7 pc . as with several other y dwarf discoveries , this object is detected by wise only in bands w2 and w3 and not in w1 or w4 ( table  [ wise_photometry_discoveries ] ) .      the @xmath21-band spectrum of this object best fits the t9 standard , but there are discrepancies at @xmath29 and @xmath34 bands . at @xmath29 band",

    "this object has the near - infrared spectrum of a normal l9 dwarf , but its wise color of w1-w2 = 0.825@xmath60.046 is markedly redder than the other l9 dwarfs on figure  [ w1w2_vs_type ] . the _",
    "spitzer_/irac color of ch1-ch2 = 0.247@xmath60.025 is redder than all other l and early - t dwarfs in figure  [ ch1ch2_vs_type ] .",
    "effects such as low - gravity or low - metallicity would cause the near - infrared spectrum of this object to appear unusually red or unusually blue , respectively , in the near - infrared ( @xcite ) , and this is not seen .",
    "one hypothesis is that this object is an unresolved l+t binary , but not one with such a warm t dwarf that the near - infrared spectrum of the composite shows itself to be peculiar .",
    "we can test this as follows .",
    "the w1-w2 color of wise 2327@xmath22730 is @xmath50.23 mag redder than the mean w1-w2 for other l9 dwarfs . using the absolute w2 versus spectral type plot of figure  [ mw2_vs_type ] along with the trend of w1-w2 color with spectral type in figure  [ w1w2_vs_type ]",
    ", we estimate that the type of the hypothesized companion would have to be roughly t6.5 .",
    "however , as figure 4 of @xcite shows , an object with a composite type of @xmath5l9 and secondary of @xmath5t6.5 would have a noticeably peculiar near - infrared spectrum which would distinguish it from a normal l9 .",
    "hence , binarity appears not to be the cause of the redder w1-w2 and ch1-ch2 colors .",
    "the reason for this color peculiarity remains unexplained .",

  "abstract_text": [
    "<S> we present ground - based spectroscopic verification of six y dwarfs ( see also cushing et al . ) , eighty - nine t dwarfs , eight l dwarfs , and one m dwarf identified by the wide - field infrared survey explorer ( wise ) . </S>",
    "<S> eighty of these are cold brown dwarfs with spectral types @xmath0t6 , six of which have been announced earlier in mainzer et al .  and burgasser et al . </S>",
    "<S> we present color - color and color - type diagrams showing the locus of m , l , t , and y dwarfs in wise color space . </S>",
    "<S> near - infrared and , in a few cases , optical spectra are presented for these discoveries . </S>",
    "<S> near - infrared classifications as late as early y are presented and objects with peculiar spectra are discussed . using these new discoveries </S>",
    "<S> , we are also able to extend the optical t dwarf classification scheme from t8 to t9 . after deriving an absolute wise 4.6 @xmath1 m ( w2 ) magnitude vs.  spectral type relation </S>",
    "<S> , we estimate spectrophotometric distances to our discoveries . </S>",
    "<S> we also use available astrometric measurements to provide preliminary trigonometric parallaxes to four our discoveries , which have types of l9 pec ( red ) , t8 , t9 , and y0 ; all of these lie within 10 pc of the sun . </S>",
    "<S> the y0 dwarf , wise 1541@xmath22250 , is the closest at @xmath3 pc ; if this 2.8 pc value persists after continued monitoring , wise 1541@xmath22250 will become the seventh closest stellar system to the sun . </S>",
    "<S> another ten objects , with types between t6 and @xmath4y0 , have spectrophotometric distance estimates also placing them within 10 pc . </S>",
    "<S> the closest of these , the t6 dwarf wise 1506 + 7027 , is believed to fall at a distance of @xmath54.9 pc . </S>",
    "<S> wise multi - epoch positions supplemented with positional info primarily from _ spitzer_/irac allow us to calculate proper motions and tangential velocities for roughly one half of the new discoveries . </S>",
    "<S> this work represents the first step by wise to complete a full - sky , volume - limited census of late - t and y dwarfs . using early results from this census , we present preliminary , lower limits to the space density of these objects and discuss constraints on both the functional form of the mass function and the low - mass limit of star formation </S>"
  ]
